class="ent-tss-16bdfpw-editable" data-slate-editor="true" data-slate-node="value" contenteditable="false" zindex="-1" style="position:relative;outline:none;white-space:pre-wrap;word-wrap:break-word"><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">A new Russian-speaking forum called RAMP was launched in July 2021 and received much attention from researchers and cybercrime actors. The forum emerged at the domain that previously hosted the Babuk ransomware data leak site and later the Payload.bin leak site. KELA researched the contents of the new site and assessed its chances to succeed.
*All the forum contents are described based on what KELA observed on RAMP until July 27, 2021, when the access became was restricted.</span></span></span></p><h2 class="ent-tss-7785c4-h2" color="inherit" id="background"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Background</span></span></span></h2><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">The Babuk ransomware group came into the spotlight at the beginning of the year 2021 but the gangÂ </span></span></span><a data-slate-node="element" href="https://www.bleepingcomputer.com/news/security/babuk-ransomware-is-back-uses-new-version-on-corporate-networks/" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" class="ent-tss-p16xa7-link"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">said that their attacks have started in October 2020</span></span></span></a><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">. The group operated as ransomware-as-a-service (RaaS), and was publicly hiring affiliates on two major Russian-speaking forums, XSS and Exploit, since March 2021.
One of the gangâ€™s most notable attacks was carried out against Washington DCâ€™s Metropolitan Police Department that took place in April 2021. The gang said they had compromised the DC Policeâ€™s networks and stolen 250 GB of unencrypted files. Some of them were published on their site.</span></span></span></p><div class="ent-tss-lr6oy8-imageWrapper"><div data-slate-node="element" data-slate-void="true" Washington DCâ€™s Metropolitan Police Department" title="Babuk posts claiming to have compromised Washington DCâ€™s Metropolitan Police Department" width="680" height="320" data-lazy-src="https://entail-assets.com/kelacyber/fit-in/680x320/babukpolice-1739369705213.png"><noscript><img style="width:100% !important" loading="lazy" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20643%20406'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="LockBit 2.0 thread on RAMP" title="LockBit 2.0 thread on RAMP" width="643" height="406" data-lazy-src="https://entail-assets.com/kelacyber/fit-in/643x406/81_1-1739370154591.png"><noscript><img style="width:100% !important" loading="lazy" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" src="https://entail-assets.com/kelacyber/fit-in/643x406/81_1-1739370154591.png" alt="LockBit 2.0 thread on RAMP" title="LockBit 2.0 thread on RAMP" width="643" height="406"></noscript><button class="MuiButtonBase-root MuiIconButton-root MuiIconButton-sizeMedium ent-tss-yjupvi-expandIcon ent-tss-45-expandIcon-ref ent-css-1yxmbwk" tabindex="0" type="button"><svg class="MuiSvgIcon-root MuiSvgIcon-fontSizeMedium ent-css-vubbuv" focusable="false" aria-hidden="true" viewbox="0 0 24 24" data-testid="OpenInFullIcon"><path d="M21 11V3h-8l3.29 3.29-10 10L3 13v8h8l-3.29-3.29 10-10z"></path></svg></button></div></div> <div data-slate-spacer="true" style="height:0;color:transparent;outline:none;position:absolute"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-zero-width="z" data-slate-length="0">ï»¿</span></span></span></div></div><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Since Initial Access Brokersâ€™ services are on the rise, the forum offers a section for access listings. Moreover, in honor of the forumâ€™s launch, some accesses through Fortinet VPN were offered for free. The access listings seem to be unique; the forum moderators promised to change them periodically to avoid multiple targeting.
The forum also has a section â€œToolsâ€ for selling/sharing exploits and malware, though its contents so far do not seem to be unique. Interestingly, the Babuk builder was shared again in this section by the admin who specified that the builder works fine for encrypting/decrypting files on Windows computers. He mentioned that the VMware ESXi version does not enable users to decrypt files.
Other sections are intended for sharing articles about hacking, chatting, and discussing the forum.</span></span></span></p><h2 class="ent-tss-7785c4-h2" color="inherit" id="the-spam-incident-and-the-building-of-the-forum"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">The Spam Incident and the Building of the Forum</span></span></span></h2><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">The site, built on the FluxBB engine, experienced a spam attack. On July 23, 2021, a threat actor created a thread where he demanded a 5,000 USD ransom to avoid spamming. Apparently, the admin didnâ€™t pay the ransom and over a few coming days, multiple users were posting porn GIFs in all sections and threads in the forum. Following the incident, many users were deleted from the forum. The admin (who previously looked for someone capable of auditing the forumâ€™s security for 2,000 USD) stated the forum will be relaunched using a new engine built from scratch. First, the admin â€œcleanedâ€ the forum and deleted most of the users. On July 27, 2021, he restricted access to the forum.</span></span></span></p><div class="ent-tss-lr6oy8-imageWrapper"><div data-slate-node="element" data-slate-void="true" style="overflow:hidden;width:100%;display:flex;flex-direction:column;margin-top:30px;align-items:flex-start"><div class="ent-tss-55ybit-imageContainer"><img style="width:100% !important" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20680%20252'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="The RAMP adminâ€™s announcement of looking for a specialist to make a security audit of the forum" title="The RAMP adminâ€™s announcement of looking for a specialist to make a security audit of the forum" width="680" height="252" data-lazy-src="https://entail-assets.com/kelacyber/fit-in/680x252/rampaudit-1739370207660.png"><noscript><img style="width:100% !important" loading="lazy" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" src="https://entail-assets.com/kelacyber/fit-in/680x252/rampaudit-1739370207660.png" alt="The RAMP adminâ€™s announcement of looking for a specialist to make a security audit of the forum" title="The RAMP adminâ€™s announcement of looking for a specialist to make a security audit of the forum" width="680" height="252"></noscript><button class="MuiButtonBase-root MuiIconButton-root MuiIconButton-sizeMedium ent-tss-yjupvi-expandIcon ent-tss-45-expandIcon-ref ent-css-1yxmbwk" tabindex="0" type="button"><svg class="MuiSvgIcon-root MuiSvgIcon-fontSizeMedium ent-css-vubbuv" focusable="false" aria-hidden="true" viewbox="0 0 24 24" data-testid="OpenInFullIcon"><path d="M21 11V3h-8l3.29 3.29-10 10L3 13v8h8l-3.29-3.29 10-10z"></path></svg></button></div></div> <div data-slate-spacer="true" style="height:0;color:transparent;outline:none;position:absolute"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-zero-width="z" data-slate-length="0">ï»¿</span></span></span></div></div><h2 class="ent-tss-7785c4-h2" color="inherit" id="forums-perspectives"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">Forumâ€™s Perspectives</span></span></span></h2><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">The forum seemed to attract some interest from members of other cybercrime forums: KELA observed several users registered with the same handles as on two major Russian-speaking forums. Due to the â€œcleaningâ€ of the forum, on July 26, 2021, the number of users was 59 who seem to be the users that somehow participated in the forum discussion. During the first ten days of its existence and before the wave of spammers the number of registered users was around 350. The number of published posts was above 100.
This pace was impressive, however, after the spam incident and deleting of the users it will definitely slow down. The registration is now closed. According to a message now appearing on the homepage, on August 13, 2021, the forum will be relaunched and registration will become available based on certain conditions. Those include users registered on XSS and Exploit for more than 2 months, with more than 10 messages on a forum and a positive reputation. An alternative option is to pay a registration fee of 500 USD, which seems to be exaggerated compared to other forums. For example, a premium user on XSS costs 120 USD for a year. Moreover, Russian cybercriminals are not used to paying money for registration on forums, especially such a (relatively) big sum.
Once the forum will be relaunched, it is possible that cybercrime actors tired of the ransomware ban will try it out. So far, the welcoming of the RaaS programs and their affiliates is the only competitive advantage of RAMP. It seems it is the only factor that can attract users from other well-established forums. As for the demand of ransomware groups for Initial Access Brokers, intrusion specialists, and other partners, they can still find them on existing forums.</span></span></span></p><div class="ent-tss-lr6oy8-imageWrapper"><div data-slate-node="element" data-slate-void="true" style="overflow:hidden;width:100%;display:flex;flex-direction:column;margin-top:30px;align-items:flex-start"><div class="ent-tss-55ybit-imageContainer"><img style="width:100% !important" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" src="data:image/svg+xml,%3Csvg%20xmlns='http://www.w3.org/2000/svg'%20viewBox='0%200%20680%20359'%3E%3C/svg%3E" alt="Frontpage of RAMP as seen on July 26 and on July 27, 2021" title="Frontpage of RAMP as seen on July 26 and on July 27, 2021" width="680" height="359" data-lazy-src="https://entail-assets.com/kelacyber/fit-in/680x359/frontpages-1739370246359.png"><noscript><img style="width:100% !important" loading="lazy" class="ent-tss-15xthk0-image-image" src="https://entail-assets.com/kelacyber/fit-in/680x359/frontpages-1739370246359.png" alt="Frontpage of RAMP as seen on July 26 and on July 27, 2021" title="Frontpage of RAMP as seen on July 26 and on July 27, 2021" width="680" height="359"></noscript><button class="MuiButtonBase-root MuiIconButton-root MuiIconButton-sizeMedium ent-tss-yjupvi-expandIcon ent-tss-45-expandIcon-ref ent-css-1yxmbwk" tabindex="0" type="button"><svg class="MuiSvgIcon-root MuiSvgIcon-fontSizeMedium ent-css-vubbuv" focusable="false" aria-hidden="true" viewbox="0 0 24 24" data-testid="OpenInFullIcon"><path d="M21 11V3h-8l3.29 3.29-10 10L3 13v8h8l-3.29-3.29 10-10z"></path></svg></button></div></div> <div data-slate-spacer="true" style="height:0;color:transparent;outline:none;position:absolute"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-zero-width="z" data-slate-length="0">ï»¿</span></span></span></div></div><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:center"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><em><span data-slate-string="true">Frontpage of RAMP as seen on July 26 and on July 27, 2021</span></em></span></span></p><p data-slate-node="element" class="ent-tss-15cp3ar-paragraph" style="text-align:left"><span data-slate-node="text"><span data-slate-leaf="true"><span data-slate-string="true">The success of the forum also depends on the interest of ransomware groups in publicly recruiting affiliates again. Some players (like Avaddon and REvil) closed their RaaS or disappeared from the public space. However, there are new groups that can use a new community to promote their RaaS. If the admins can leverage their competitive advantage of welcoming RaaS programs, chances to grow are fairly high.

The forum emerged at the domain that previously hosted the Babuk ransomware data leak site and later the Payload.bin leak site. KELA researched the contents of the new site and assessed its chances to succeed.\n*All the forum contents are described based on what KELA observed on RAMP until July 27, 2021, when the access became was restricted.\nBackground\nThe Babuk ransomware group came into the spotlight at the beginning of the year 2021 but the gangÂ said that their attacks have started in October 2020. The group operated as ransomware-as-a-service (RaaS), and was publicly hiring affiliates on two major Russian-speaking forums, XSS and Exploit, since March 2021.\nOne of the gangâ€™s most notable attacks was carried out against Washington DCâ€™s Metropolitan Police Department that took place in April 2021. The gang said they had compromised the DC Policeâ€™s networks and stolen 250 GB of unencrypted files. Some of them were published on their site.\n\nBabuk posts claiming to have compromised Washington DCâ€™s Metropolitan Police Department\nShortly after the attack, the chaos surrounding the Babuk RaaS closure started. First, the gang stated it is closing the operation and promised to publish the source code of its malware to enable other threat actors to create their own ransomware. Then, the Babuk ransomware developers deleted the post and published a new announcement claiming they plan to continue breaching companies but instead of stealing sensitive files and encrypting local data, the group plans only to steal it. However, that second announcement was also deleted. On May 15, 2021, the Babuk representative stated on one of the forums that their RaaS affiliate program was closed.\n\nBabuk announcements of coming changes of their leak site and RaaS\nOn June 1, 2021, KELA observed several changes in the content and appearance of the Babuk site. The domain used by Babuk showed a page titled â€œPayload.binâ€ with the following message on the front page: â€œWelcome to Leaks site created by Payload.bin.â€ It appeared that this Payload.bin site was the promised site for leaking the stolen data.\nHowever, only one victim was listed on the site â€“ Polish game developer CD Projekt Red. Interestingly enough, the company fell victim to HelloKitty ransomware in February 2021. Then, the data allegedly stolen during the attack was traded on an auction on the cybercrime forum Exploit. The sellers claimed the data was sold outside of the forum. Interestingly, one of the RAMP users asked about the origins of this leak being posted on Payload.bin. The admin claimed the Babuk gang did not attack the company and they just provided a place for the leak: â€œThe Babuk team never had anything to do with this project, we were just asked to post it, so I provided the material as it is.â€\n\nThe leak of CD Projektâ€™s data on Payload.bin and an explanation of this leak on RAMP\nOn June 27, 2021, a builder (source code) for the Babuk ransomware wasÂ uploadedÂ to VirusTotal. This builder could be used to create custom versions of the Babuk ransomware and generate decrypters. Researchers speculated the code could be leaked by former members of the groups or rivals.\nOn July 1, 2021, it became known that Babuk launched a new leak site stating the operation continues under the name Babuk 2.0. The gang claimed the old version of Babuk ransomware was leaked, while the new version is being used in ongoing attacks.\nOn July 12, 2021, KELA noticed that the former Babuk ransomware gangâ€™s leak site had changed again and was now hosting a forum named RAMP. A new admin initially named TetyaSluha (now Orange) announced it is now a place where ransomware affiliates can be protected from unscrupulous RaaS programs. The admin claimed that following the ransomware ban on other forums, he wanted to create a new community. The name of the new forum is a reference to the now-defunct Russian Anonymous Marketplace (a drug market that closed in 2017). So the big question comes down to:Â Whatâ€™s in this â€œmarketplaceâ€?\nThe Adminâ€™s Connections to Babuk\nThe fact that the RAMP site is hosted on the same domain that once was Babukâ€™s leak site and then Payload.bin hints that the administrator is somehow related to Babuk. On May 13, 2021, in the post promising to leak the data of Washington DCâ€™s Metropolitan Police Department, the author stated: â€œI handed over the source code to another team, which will continue to develop the product under a different brand, I remain the only owner of the domain and blog, my service will continue to develop.â€ It seems that the post author is the future admin of Payload.bin and RAMP.\n\nAnnouncement about handing over source code and remaining an owner of the domain, most likely written by the current RAMP admin\nWhen announcing the forumâ€™s opening, the admin stated: â€œ[If you want to know â€“ KELA]Â who I am you can search online for the babuk key.â€ The mention of â€œBabuk keyâ€ probably meant the builder leak mentioned above. In addition, the admin said: â€œAll this activity that grew into the RAMP forum is the result of my yearâ€™-long work in the field and the competent manipulation of journalists from top outlets, such as Bloomberg, and so on. I promoted this domain through blood and sweat.â€ This again implies that the admin was involved in the Babuk operation from the beginning.\n\nThe RAMP adminâ€™s announcement about the RAMP launch and his affiliation with the Babuk team and the domain\nMoreover, when sharing the Babuk builder on RAMP, the admin claimed: â€œA guy who made Babuk for me just took the Darkside ESX locker and reversed it. I canâ€™t tell if there is a problem with the ESX [version] because Iâ€™ve used it only for three companies.â€ From this and other posts sharing insights on how to attack the companyâ€™s network, we can suggest that the admin was conducting ransomware attacks by himself.\nThe admin said that now he is not affiliated with the gang and even stated: â€œI recommend to blacklist this product to all security firms and data security [specialists].â€\n\nThe RAMP adminâ€™s post about the Babuk ESXi version being based on the DarkSide ESXi version\nRAMP Forumâ€™s Contents\nThe new forum is Russian-speaking and named RAMP in honor of the now-defunct Russian drug marketplace, but its purpose is far away from selling drugs. The admin who renamed himself to Orange (the old RAMPâ€™s adminâ€™s handle) claimed the forum will be a community for various cybercriminals, including ransomware developers and affiliatesÂ recently banned onÂ XSS and Exploit. He stated the forumâ€™s full name is â€œRansom Anon Mark Place.â€\nRules of the forum stated that members are prohibited from attacking Russia and CIS countries (which isÂ common for such forums), using multiple accounts, spamming, and performing some other actions. Curiously, the moderators claimed it is prohibited to propagate â€œdifferent actions going against Criminal Code of RF [Russian Federation].â€\n\nRAMP rules\nThe forum has multiple sections typical for such cybercrime forums, with a general notice â€œwelcomingâ€ both RaaS and other services. Two sections that attract a particular interest are called â€œVendorâ€ and â€œAffiliate Programsâ€ â€“ they are intended for â€œpeople and services in which we [administration â€“ KELA] and our community trust.â€ As such, KELA observed a thread dedicated to the LockBit 2.0 affiliate program thread. In the thread, a user named LockBit (most likely the gangâ€™s representative) claimed he will launch the LockBit 2.0 ransomware ESXi version soon.\n\nSince Initial Access Brokersâ€™ services are on the rise, the forum offers a section for access listings. Moreover, in honor of the forumâ€™s launch, some accesses through Fortinet VPN were offered for free. The access listings seem to be unique; the forum moderators promised to change them periodically to avoid multiple targeting.\nThe forum also has a section â€œToolsâ€ for selling\u002Fsharing exploits and malware, though its contents so far do not seem to be unique. Interestingly, the Babuk builder was shared again in this section by the admin who specified that the builder works fine for encrypting\u002Fdecrypting files on Windows computers. He mentioned that the VMware ESXi version does not enable users to decrypt files.\nOther sections are intended for sharing articles about hacking, chatting, and discussing the forum.\nThe Spam Incident and the Building of the Forum\nThe site, built on the FluxBB engine, experienced a spam attack. On July 23, 2021, a threat actor created a thread where he demanded a 5,000 USD ransom to avoid spamming. Apparently, the admin didnâ€™t pay the ransom and over a few coming days, multiple users were posting porn GIFs in all sections and threads in the forum. Following the incident, many users were deleted from the forum. The admin (who previously looked for someone capable of auditing the forumâ€™s security for 2,000 USD) stated the forum will be relaunched using a new engine built from scratch. First, the admin â€œcleanedâ€ the forum and deleted most of the users. On July 27, 2021, he restricted access to the forum.\n\nForumâ€™s Perspectives\nThe forum seemed to attract some interest from members of other cybercrime forums: KELA observed several users registered with the same handles as on two major Russian-speaking forums. Due to the â€œcleaningâ€ of the forum, on July 26, 2021, the number of users was 59 who seem to be the users that somehow participated in the forum discussion. During the first ten days of its existence and before the wave of spammers the number of registered users was around 350. The number of published posts was above 100.\nThis pace was impressive, however, after the spam incident and deleting of the users it will definitely slow down. The registration is now closed. According to a message now appearing on the homepage, on August 13, 2021, the forum will be relaunched and registration will become available based on certain conditions. Those include users registered on XSS and Exploit for more than 2 months, with more than 10 messages on a forum and a positive reputation. An alternative option is to pay a registration fee of 500 USD, which seems to be exaggerated compared to other forums. For example, a premium user on XSS costs 120 USD for a year. Moreover, Russian cybercriminals are not used to paying money for registration on forums, especially such a (relatively) big sum.\nOnce the forum will be relaunched, it is possible that cybercrime actors tired of the ransomware ban will try it out. So far, the welcoming of the RaaS programs and their affiliates is the only competitive advantage of RAMP. It seems it is the only factor that can attract users from other well-established forums. As for the demand of ransomware groups for Initial Access Brokers, intrusion specialists, and other partners, they can still find them on existing forums.\n\nFrontpage of RAMP as seen on July 26 and on July 27, 2021\nThe success of the forum also depends on the interest of ransomware groups in publicly recruiting affiliates again. Some players (like Avaddon and REvil) closed their RaaS or disappeared from the public space. However, there are new groups that can use a new community to promote their RaaS. If the admins can leverage their competitive advantage of welcoming RaaS programs, chances to grow are fairly high.\n","richText":"[{\"type\":\"paragraph\",\"children\":[{\"text\":\"A new Russian-speaking forum called RAMP was launched in July 2021 and received much attention from researchers and cybercrime actors. Moreover, Russian cybercriminals are not used to paying money for registration on forums, especially such a (relatively) big sum.\\nOnce the forum will be relaunched, it is possible that cybercrime actors tired of the ransomware ban will try it out. So far, the welcoming of the RaaS programs and their affiliates is the only competitive advantage of RAMP. It seems it is the only factor that can attract users from other well-established forums. As for the demand of ransomware groups for Initial Access Brokers, intrusion specialists, and other partners, they can still find them on existing forums.\"}]},{\"type\":\"image\",\"file\":{\"externalId\":null,\"_id\":\"67acaf06f11780c2da9fad6f\",\"fileName\":\"kelacyber\u002Ffrontpages-1739370246359\",\"url\":\"https:\u002F\u002Fsun-assets.s3.eu-west-1.amazonaws.com\u002Fkelacyber\u002Ffrontpages-1739370246359.png\",\"cdnUrl\":\"https:\u002F\u002Fentail-assets.com\u002Fkelacyber\u002Ffrontpages-1739370246359.png\",\"thumbnailUrl\":\"https:\u002F\u002Fentail-assets.com\u002Ffit-in\u002F200x200\u002Fkelacyber\u002Ffrontpages-1739370246359.png\",\"mimeType\":\"image\u002Fpng\",\"extType\":\"png\",\"hash\":\"\\\"17f1aff8a1188c10e5d21b69652af133\\\"\",\"height\":471,\"width\":894,\"desiredWidth\":894,\"size\":\"100283\",\"bucket\":\"sun-assets\",\"key\":\"kelacyber\u002Ffrontpages-1739370246359.png\",\"website\":\"67583e08a0365cb3a8090712\",\"createdAt\":\"2025-02-12T14:24:06.408Z\",\"updatedAt\":\"2025-02-12T14:24:15.471Z\",\"__v\":0,\"alt\":\"Frontpage of RAMP as seen on July 26 and on July 27, 2021\",\"caption\":\"a computer screen with a red and white text on it\",\"title\":\"Frontpage of RAMP as seen on July 26 and on July 27, 2021\"},\"uuid\":\"3d920743-7231-4424-b891-9cdfb9240ed9\",\"children\":[{\"text\":\"\"}]},{\"type\":\"paragraph\",\"children\":[{\"text\":\"Frontpage of RAMP as seen on July 26 and on July 27, 2021\",\"italic\":true}],\"alignment\":\"center\"},{\"type\":\"paragraph\",\"children\":[{\"text\":\"The success of the forum also depends on the interest of ransomware groups in publicly recruiting affiliates again.             <script>

        // if getParameterByName function is not defined, define it
        if (typeof getParameterByName === 'undefined') {
            function getParameterByName(name, url) {
                if (!url) url = window.location.href;
                name = name.replace(/[\[\]]/g, "\\$&");
                var regex = new RegExp("[?&]" + name + "(=([^&#]*)|&|#|$)"),
                    results = regex.exec(url);
                if (!results) return null;
                if (!results[2]) return '';
                return decodeURIComponent(results[2].replace(/\+/g, " "));
            }
        }

        jQuery(document).ready(function($) {

            // First detect if _GET params are present.
            // We only need utm_source, utm_medium and utm_campaign
            var utm_source = getParameterByName('utm_source');
            var utm_medium = getParameterByName('utm_medium');
            var utm_campaign = getParameterByName('utm_campaign');
            var utm_content = getParameterByName('utm_content');
            var utm_term = getParameterByName('utm_term');

            // Next we will use Cookies.js to set cookies

            // If _GET params are present, set cookies
            if (utm_source) {
                Cookies.set('kela_utm_source', utm_source, { expires: 1, path: '/' });
            }
            if (utm_medium) {
                Cookies.set('kela_utm_medium', utm_medium, { expires: 1, path: '/' });
            }
            if (utm_campaign) {
                Cookies.set('kela_utm_campaign', utm_campaign, { expires: 1, path: '/' });
            }
            if (utm_content) {
                Cookies.set('kela_utm_content', utm_content, { expires: 1, path: '/' });
            }
            if (utm_term) {
                Cookies.set('kela_utm_term', utm_term, { expires: 1, path: '/' });
            }

            // Check if cookies are present
            if (Cookies.get('kela_utm_source')) {
                utm_source = Cookies.get('kela_utm_source');
            }
            if (Cookies.get('kela_utm_medium')) {
                utm_medium = Cookies.get('kela_utm_medium');
            }
            if (Cookies.get('kela_utm_campaign')) {
                utm_campaign = Cookies.get('kela_utm_campaign');
            }
            if (Cookies.get('kela_utm_content')) {
                utm_content = Cookies.get('kela_utm_content');
            }
            if (Cookies.get('kela_utm_term')) {
                utm_term = Cookies.get('kela_utm_term');
            }

            // Wait 4 seconds for the form to load
            setTimeout(function() {
                
                // Find if hidden fields exist, for example: .hs-utm_campaign input
                if ($(".hs-utm_source input").length) {
                    $(".hs-utm_source input").val(utm_source);
                }
                if ($(".hs-utm_medium input").length) {
                    $(".hs-utm_medium input").val(utm_medium);
                }   

                if ($(".hs-utm_campaign input").length) {
                    $(".hs-utm_campaign input").val(utm_campaign);
                }

                if ($(".hs-utm_content input").length) {
                    $(".hs-utm_content input").val(utm_content);
                }

                if ($(".hs-utm_term input").length) {
                    $(".hs-utm_term input").val(utm_term);
                }

                if ($(".gfield--type-text.utm_source input").length) {
                    $(".gfield--type-text.utm_source input").val(utm_source);
                }

                if ($(".gfield--type-text.utm_medium input").length) {
                    $(".gfield--type-text.utm_medium input").val(utm_medium);
                }

                if ($(".gfield--type-text.utm_campaign input").length) {
                    $(".gfield--type-text.utm_campaign input").val(utm_campaign);
                }

                if ($(".gfield--type-text.utm_content input").length) {
                    $(".gfield--type-text.utm_content input").val(utm_content);
                }

                if ($(".gfield--type-text.utm_term input").length) {
                    $(".gfield--type-text.utm_term input").val(utm_term);
                }
                
            }, 4000);

            
        });
    </script>
